---
collectionId: "9ktkng9a95n6199"
collectionName: "projects"
created: "2023-06-15 03:33:44.665Z"
description: "<p><strong>Palantir Technologies</strong> is a <a title=\"Public company\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Public_company\">public</a> American company that specializes in <a title=\"Big data\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Big_data\">big data</a> <a title=\"Analytics\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Analytics\">analytics</a>. Headquartered in <a class=\"mw-redirect\" title=\"Denver, Colorado\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Denver,_Colorado\">Denver, Colorado</a>, it was founded by <a title=\"Peter Thiel\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Peter_Thiel\">Peter Thiel</a>,<sup id=\"cite_ref-3\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Palantir_Technologies#cite_note-3\">[3]</a></sup> Nathan Gettings, Joe Lonsdale, <a title=\"Stephen Cohen (entrepreneur)\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Stephen_Cohen_(entrepreneur)\">Stephen Cohen</a>, and <a title=\"Alex Karp\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alex_Karp\">Alex Karp</a> in 2003. The company's name is derived from <em><a title=\"The Lord of the Rings\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_Lord_of_the_Rings\">The Lord of the Rings</a></em> where the magical <em><a class=\"mw-redirect\" title=\"Palant&iacute;ri\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Palant%C3%ADri\">palant&iacute;ri</a></em> were \"seeing-stones,\" described as indestructible balls of crystal used for communication and to see events in other parts of the world.</p>\r\n<p>The company is known for three projects in particular: Palantir Gotham, Palantir Apollo, and Palantir Foundry. Palantir Gotham is used by <a class=\"mw-redirect\" title=\"Counter-terrorism\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Counter-terrorism\">counter-terrorism</a> analysts at offices in the <a title=\"United States Intelligence Community\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States_Intelligence_Community\">United States Intelligence Community</a> (USIC) and <a title=\"United States Department of Defense\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States_Department_of_Defense\">United States Department of Defense</a>.<sup id=\"cite_ref-4\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Palantir_Technologies#cite_note-4\">[4]</a></sup> In the past, Gotham was used by fraud investigators at the <a title=\"Recovery Accountability and Transparency Board\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Recovery_Accountability_and_Transparency_Board\">Recovery Accountability and Transparency Board</a>, a former US federal agency which operated from 2009 to 2015. Gotham was also used by cyber analysts at <a title=\"Information Warfare Monitor\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Information_Warfare_Monitor\">Information Warfare Monitor</a>, a Canadian public-private venture which operated from 2003 to 2012. Palantir Apollo is the operating system for continuous delivery and deployment across all environments.<sup id=\"cite_ref-5\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Palantir_Technologies#cite_note-5\">[5]</a></sup> Their SaaS is one of five offerings authorized for Mission Critical National Security Systems (IL5) by the U.S. Department of Defense.<sup id=\"cite_ref-bare_url_6-0\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Palantir_Technologies#cite_note-bare_url-6\">[6]</a></sup><sup id=\"cite_ref-npr_7-0\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Palantir_Technologies#cite_note-npr-7\">[7]</a></sup> Palantir Foundry is used by corporate clients such as <a title=\"Morgan Stanley\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Morgan_Stanley\">Morgan Stanley</a>, <a class=\"mw-redirect\" title=\"Merck KGaA\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Merck_KGaA\">Merck KGaA</a>, <a title=\"Airbus\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Airbus\">Airbus</a>, <a title=\"Wejo\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wejo\">Wejo</a>, <a title=\"Lilium GmbH\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lilium_GmbH\">Lilium</a>, and <a title=\"Fiat Chrysler Automobiles\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fiat_Chrysler_Automobiles\">Fiat Chrysler Automobiles</a>.<sup id=\"cite_ref-8\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Palantir_Technologies#cite_note-8\">[8]</a></sup></p>\r\n<p>Palantir's original clients were federal agencies of the <a title=\"United States Intelligence Community\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States_Intelligence_Community\">USIC</a>. It has since expanded its customer base to serve state and local governments, as well as private companies in the financial and healthcare industries.<sup id=\"cite_ref-historypalantir_9-0\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Palantir_Technologies#cite_note-historypalantir-9\">[9]</a></sup></p>\r\n<h2><span id=\"History\" class=\"mw-headline\">History</span></h2>\r\n<h3><span id=\"2003.E2.80.932008:_Founding_and_early_years\"></span><span id=\"2003&ndash;2008:_Founding_and_early_years\" class=\"mw-headline\">2003&ndash;2008: Founding and early years</span></h3>\r\n<div class=\"thumbinner\" style=\"width: 202px;\"><a class=\"image\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Peter_Thiel_TechCrunch50.jpg\"><img class=\"thumbimage\" src=\"https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e6/Peter_Thiel_TechCrunch50.jpg/200px-Peter_Thiel_TechCrunch50.jpg\" srcset=\"//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e6/Peter_Thiel_TechCrunch50.jpg/300px-Peter_Thiel_TechCrunch50.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e6/Peter_Thiel_TechCrunch50.jpg/400px-Peter_Thiel_TechCrunch50.jpg 2x\" width=\"200\" height=\"300\" data-file-width=\"683\" data-file-height=\"1024\"></a>\r\n<div class=\"thumbcaption\">\r\n<div class=\"magnify\">&nbsp;</div>\r\n</div>\r\n</div>\r\n<div class=\"thumb tright\">\r\n<div class=\"thumbinner\" style=\"width: 202px;\">\r\n<div class=\"thumbcaption\">Founder and chairman <a title=\"Peter Thiel\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Peter_Thiel\">Peter Thiel</a> was Palantir's largest shareholder as of late 2014.</div>\r\n</div>\r\n</div>\r\n<p>Though usually listed as having been founded in 2004, <a title=\"U.S. Securities and Exchange Commission\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/U.S._Securities_and_Exchange_Commission\">SEC</a> filings state Palantir's official incorporation to be in May 2003 by <a title=\"Peter Thiel\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Peter_Thiel\">Peter Thiel</a> (co-founder of <a title=\"PayPal\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/PayPal\">PayPal</a>), who named the start-up after the \"<a title=\"Palant&iacute;r\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Palant%C3%ADr\">seeing stone</a>\" in <a title=\"Tolkien's legendarium\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tolkien%27s_legendarium\">Tolkien's legendarium</a>.<sup id=\"cite_ref-historypalantir_9-1\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Palantir_Technologies#cite_note-historypalantir-9\">[9]</a></sup> Thiel saw Palantir as a \"mission-oriented company\" which could apply software similar to PayPal's fraud recognition systems to \"reduce terrorism while preserving civil liberties.\"<sup id=\"cite_ref-10\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Palantir_Technologies#cite_note-10\">[10]</a></sup></p>\r\n<p>In 2004, Thiel bankrolled the creation of a prototype by <a title=\"PayPal\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/PayPal\">PayPal</a> engineer Nathan Gettings and <a title=\"Stanford University\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Stanford_University\">Stanford University</a> students Joe Lonsdale and <a title=\"Stephen Cohen (entrepreneur)\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Stephen_Cohen_(entrepreneur)\">Stephen Cohen</a>. That same year, Thiel hired <a title=\"Alex Karp\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alex_Karp\">Alex Karp</a>, a former colleague of his from <a title=\"Stanford Law School\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Stanford_Law_School\">Stanford Law School</a>, as <a title=\"Chief executive officer\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chief_executive_officer\">chief executive officer</a>.<sup id=\"cite_ref-11\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Palantir_Technologies#cite_note-11\">[11]</a></sup></p>\r\n<p>Headquartered in <a title=\"Palo Alto, California\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Palo_Alto,_California\">Palo Alto, California</a>, the company initially struggled to find investors. According to Karp, <a title=\"Sequoia Capital\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sequoia_Capital\">Sequoia Capital</a> chairman <a title=\"Michael Moritz\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Michael_Moritz\">Michael Moritz</a> doodled through an entire meeting, and a <a title=\"Kleiner Perkins\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kleiner_Perkins\">Kleiner Perkins</a> executive lectured the founders about the inevitable failure of their company.<sup id=\"cite_ref-12\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Palantir_Technologies#cite_note-12\">[12]</a></sup> The only early investments were $2 million from the U.S. <a title=\"Central Intelligence Agency\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Central_Intelligence_Agency\">Central Intelligence Agency</a>'s venture capital arm <a title=\"In-Q-Tel\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/In-Q-Tel\">In-Q-Tel</a>, and $30 million from Thiel himself and his venture capital firm, <a title=\"Founders Fund\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Founders_Fund\">Founders Fund</a>.<sup id=\"cite_ref-bare_url_6-1\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Palantir_Technologies#cite_note-bare_url-6\">[6]</a></sup><sup id=\"cite_ref-npr_7-1\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Palantir_Technologies#cite_note-npr-7\">[7]</a></sup><sup id=\"cite_ref-13\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Palantir_Technologies#cite_note-13\">[13]</a></sup><sup id=\"cite_ref-14\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Palantir_Technologies#cite_note-14\">[14]</a></sup><sup id=\"cite_ref-charlierose_15-0\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Palantir_Technologies#cite_note-charlierose-15\">[15]</a></sup></p>\r\n<p>Palantir developed its technology by computer scientists and analysts from intelligence agencies over three years, through pilots facilitated by In-Q-Tel.<sup id=\"cite_ref-16\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Palantir_Technologies#cite_note-16\">[16]</a></sup><sup id=\"cite_ref-bare_url_6-2\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Palantir_Technologies#cite_note-bare_url-6\">[6]</a></sup> The company stated computers alone using <a title=\"Artificial intelligence\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_intelligence\">artificial intelligence</a> could not defeat an adaptive adversary. Instead, Palantir proposed using human analysts to explore data from many sources, called <a title=\"Intelligence amplification\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Intelligence_amplification\">intelligence augmentation</a>.<sup id=\"cite_ref-17\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Palantir_Technologies#cite_note-17\">[17]</a></sup></p>\r\n<h3><span id=\"2009:_GhostNet_and_the_Shadow_Network\" class=\"mw-headline\">2009: GhostNet and the Shadow Network</span></h3>\r\n<p>In 2009 and 2010 respectively, <a title=\"Information Warfare Monitor\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Information_Warfare_Monitor\">Information Warfare Monitor</a> used Palantir software to uncover the <a title=\"GhostNet\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/GhostNet\">GhostNet</a> and the <a title=\"Shadow Network\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Shadow_Network\">Shadow Network</a>. The GhostNet was a China-based cyber espionage network targeting 1,295 computers in 103 countries, including the <a title=\"Dalai Lama\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dalai_Lama\">Dalai Lama</a>&rsquo;s office, a <a title=\"NATO\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/NATO\">NATO</a> computer and various national embassies.<sup id=\"cite_ref-18\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Palantir_Technologies#cite_note-18\">[18]</a></sup> The Shadow Network was also a China-based espionage operation that hacked into the Indian security and defense apparatus. Cyber spies stole documents related to Indian security and NATO troop activity in Afghanistan.<sup id=\"cite_ref-bare_url_a_19-0\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Palantir_Technologies#cite_note-bare_url_a-19\">[19]</a></sup><sup id=\"cite_ref-Markoff_20-0\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Palantir_Technologies#cite_note-Markoff-20\">[20]</a></sup></p>\r\n<h3><span id=\"2010.E2.80.932012:_Expansion\"></span><span id=\"2010&ndash;2012:_Expansion\" class=\"mw-headline\">2010&ndash;2012: Expansion</span></h3>\r\n<p>In April 2010, Palantir announced a partnership with <a title=\"Thomson Reuters\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Thomson_Reuters\">Thomson Reuters</a> to sell the Palantir Metropolis product as \"QA Studio\" (a <a title=\"Quantitative research\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Quantitative_research\">quantitative analysis</a> tool).<sup id=\"cite_ref-21\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Palantir_Technologies#cite_note-21\">[21]</a></sup> On June 18, 2010, <a title=\"Vice President of the United States\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vice_President_of_the_United_States\">Vice President</a> <a title=\"Joe Biden\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Joe_Biden\">Joe Biden</a> and <a title=\"Office of Management and Budget\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Office_of_Management_and_Budget\">Office of Management and Budget</a> Director <a class=\"mw-redirect\" title=\"Peter Orszag\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Peter_Orszag\">Peter Orszag</a> held a press conference at the <a title=\"White House\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/White_House\">White House</a> announcing the success of fighting fraud in the stimulus by the <a title=\"Recovery Accountability and Transparency Board\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Recovery_Accountability_and_Transparency_Board\">Recovery Accountability and Transparency Board</a> (RATB). Biden credited the success to the software, Palantir, being deployed by the federal government.<sup id=\"cite_ref-22\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Palantir_Technologies#cite_note-22\">[22]</a></sup> He announced that the capability will be deployed at other government agencies, starting with <a title=\"Medicare (United States)\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Medicare_(United_States)\">Medicare</a> and <a title=\"Medicaid\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Medicaid\">Medicaid</a>.<sup id=\"cite_ref-23\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Palantir_Technologies#cite_note-23\">[23]</a></sup><sup id=\"cite_ref-24\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Palantir_Technologies#cite_note-24\">[24]</a></sup><sup id=\"cite_ref-bare_url_b_25-0\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Palantir_Technologies#cite_note-bare_url_b-25\">[25]</a></sup><sup id=\"cite_ref-26\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Palantir_Technologies#cite_note-26\">[26]</a></sup></p>\r\n<p>Estimates were $250 million in revenues in 2011.<sup id=\"cite_ref-27\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Palantir_Technologies#cite_note-27\">[27]</a></sup></p>\r\n<h3><span id=\"2013.E2.80.932016:_Additional_funding\"></span><span id=\"2013&ndash;2016:_Additional_funding\" class=\"mw-headline\">2013&ndash;2016: Additional funding</span></h3>\r\n<table class=\"toccolours\" style=\"float: right; margin-left: 1em; margin-right: 0em; font-size: 85%; background: offwhite; color: black; width: 30em; max-width: 60%;\" cellspacing=\"5\">\r\n<tbody>\r\n<tr>\r\n<td style=\"text-align: left;\">\"[As of 2013] the U.S. spy agencies also employed Palantir to connect databases across departments. Before this, most of the databases used by the CIA and FBI were <a title=\"Information silo\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Information_silo\">siloed</a>, forcing users to search each database individually. Now everything is linked together using Palantir.\"</td>\r\n</tr>\r\n<tr>\r\n<td style=\"text-align: left;\">&mdash; <a title=\"TechCrunch\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TechCrunch\">TechCrunch</a> in January 2015<sup id=\"cite_ref-tebtecnchrun_28-0\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Palantir_Technologies#cite_note-tebtecnchrun-28\">[28]</a></sup></td>\r\n</tr>\r\n</tbody>\r\n</table>\r\n<p>A document leaked to <a title=\"TechCrunch\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TechCrunch\">TechCrunch</a> revealed that Palantir's clients as of 2013 included at least twelve groups within the U.S. government, including the <a title=\"Central Intelligence Agency\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Central_Intelligence_Agency\">CIA</a>, the <a title=\"United States Department of Homeland Security\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States_Department_of_Homeland_Security\">DHS</a>, the <a title=\"National Security Agency\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/National_Security_Agency\">NSA</a>, the <a title=\"Federal Bureau of Investigation\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Federal_Bureau_of_Investigation\">FBI</a>, the <a title=\"Centers for Disease Control and Prevention\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Centers_for_Disease_Control_and_Prevention\">CDC</a>, the <a title=\"United States Marine Corps\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States_Marine_Corps\">Marine Corps</a>, the <a title=\"United States Air Force\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States_Air_Force\">Air Force</a>, the <a title=\"United States Special Operations Command\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States_Special_Operations_Command\">Special Operations Command</a>, the <a class=\"mw-redirect\" title=\"West Point\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/West_Point\">United States Military Academy</a>, the <a title=\"Joint Improvised-Threat Defeat Organization\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Joint_Improvised-Threat_Defeat_Organization\">Joint Improvised-Threat Defeat Organization</a> and Allies, the <a title=\"Recovery Accountability and Transparency Board\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Recovery_Accountability_and_Transparency_Board\">Recovery Accountability and Transparency Board</a> and the <a class=\"mw-redirect\" title=\"National Center for Missing and Exploited Children\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/National_Center_for_Missing_and_Exploited_Children\">National Center for Missing and Exploited Children</a>. However, at the time, the <a title=\"United States Army\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States_Army\">United States Army</a> continued to use its own data analysis tool.<sup id=\"cite_ref-tebtecnchrun_28-1\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Palantir_Technologies#cite_note-tebtecnchrun-28\">[28]</a></sup> Also, according to <a title=\"TechCrunch\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TechCrunch\">TechCrunch</a>, the U.S. spy agencies such as the CIA and FBI were linked for the first time with Palantir software, as their databases had previously been \"<a title=\"Information silo\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Information_silo\">siloed</a>.\"<sup id=\"cite_ref-tebtecnchrun_28-2\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Palantir_Technologies#cite_note-tebtecnchrun-28\">[28]</a></sup></p>\r\n<p>In September 2013, Palantir disclosed over $196 million in funding according to a U.S. <a class=\"mw-redirect\" title=\"Securities and Exchange Commission\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Securities_and_Exchange_Commission\">Securities and Exchange Commission</a> filing.<sup id=\"cite_ref-29\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Palantir_Technologies#cite_note-29\">[29]</a></sup><sup id=\"cite_ref-30\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Palantir_Technologies#cite_note-30\">[30]</a></sup> It was estimated that the company would likely close almost $1 billion in contracts in 2014.<sup id=\"cite_ref-31\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Palantir_Technologies#cite_note-31\">[31]</a></sup> CEO <a title=\"Alex Karp\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alex_Karp\">Alex Karp</a> announced in 2013 that the company would not be pursuing an <a class=\"mw-redirect\" title=\"IPO\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/IPO\">IPO</a>, as going public would make \"running a company like ours very difficult.\"<sup id=\"cite_ref-teafunding_32-0\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Palantir_Technologies#cite_note-teafunding-32\">[32]</a></sup> In December 2013, the company began a round of financing, raising around $450 million from private funders. This raised the company's value to $9 billion, according to <em><a title=\"Forbes\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Forbes\">Forbes</a></em>, with the magazine further explaining that the valuation made Palantir \"among Silicon Valley&rsquo;s most valuable private technology companies.\"<sup id=\"cite_ref-teafunding_32-1\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Palantir_Technologies#cite_note-teafunding-32\">[32]</a></sup></p>\r\n<p>In December 2014, <em>Forbes</em> reported that Palantir was looking to raise $400 million in an additional round of financing, after the company filed paperwork with the <a class=\"mw-redirect\" title=\"Securities and Exchange Commission\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Securities_and_Exchange_Commission\">Securities and Exchange Commission</a> the month before. The report was based on research by VC Experts. If completed, <em>Forbes</em> stated Palantir's funding could reach a total of $1.2 billion.<sup id=\"cite_ref-teafunding_32-2\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Palantir_Technologies#cite_note-teafunding-32\">[32]</a></sup> As of December 2014, the company continued to have diverse private funders, <a title=\"Ken Langone\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ken_Langone\">Ken Langone</a> and <a title=\"Stanley Druckenmiller\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Stanley_Druckenmiller\">Stanley Druckenmiller</a>, <a title=\"In-Q-Tel\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/In-Q-Tel\">In-Q-Tel</a> of the CIA,<sup id=\"cite_ref-IranNuclearDeal_33-0\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Palantir_Technologies#cite_note-IranNuclearDeal-33\">[33]</a></sup> <a title=\"Tiger Global Management\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tiger_Global_Management\">Tiger Global Management</a>, and <a title=\"Founders Fund\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Founders_Fund\">Founders Fund</a>, which is a venture Firm operated by <a title=\"Peter Thiel\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Peter_Thiel\">Peter Thiel</a>, the chairman of Palantir. As of December 2014, Thiel was Palantir's largest shareholder.<sup id=\"cite_ref-teafunding_32-3\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Palantir_Technologies#cite_note-teafunding-32\">[32]</a></sup></p>\r\n<p>The company was valued at $15 billion in November 2014.<sup id=\"cite_ref-34\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Palantir_Technologies#cite_note-34\">[34]</a></sup> In June 2015, <a title=\"BuzzFeed\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/BuzzFeed\">BuzzFeed</a> reported the company was raising up to $500 million in new capital at a valuation of $20 billion.<sup id=\"cite_ref-35\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Palantir_Technologies#cite_note-35\">[35]</a></sup> By December 2015, it had raised a further $880 million, while the company was still valued at $20 billion.<sup id=\"cite_ref-36\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Palantir_Technologies#cite_note-36\">[36]</a></sup> In February 2016, Palantir bought Kimono Labs, a startup which makes it easy to collect information from public facing websites.<sup id=\"cite_ref-37\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Palantir_Technologies#cite_note-37\">[37]</a></sup></p>\r\n<p>In August 2016, Palantir acquired <a class=\"mw-redirect\" title=\"Data visualization\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Data_visualization\">data visualization</a> startup Silk.<sup id=\"cite_ref-38\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Palantir_Technologies#cite_note-38\">[38]</a></sup></p>\r\n<h3><span id=\"2020\" class=\"mw-headline\">2020</span></h3>\r\n<p>Palantir is one of four large technology firms<sup id=\"cite_ref-39\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Palantir_Technologies#cite_note-39\">[39]</a></sup> to start working with the <a class=\"mw-redirect\" title=\"NHS\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/NHS\">NHS</a> on supporting <a title=\"COVID-19\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/COVID-19\">COVID-19</a> efforts through the provision of software from Palantir Foundry<sup id=\"cite_ref-40\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Palantir_Technologies#cite_note-40\">[40]</a></sup> and by April 2020 several countries have used Palantir technology to track and contain the contagion.<sup id=\"cite_ref-NYT_(21_Oct_2020)_41-0\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Palantir_Technologies#cite_note-NYT_(21_Oct_2020)-41\">[41]</a></sup> Palantir also developed Tiberius, a software for vaccine allocation used in the United States.<sup id=\"cite_ref-42\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Palantir_Technologies#cite_note-42\">[42]</a></sup></p>\r\n<p>In December 2020, Palantir was awarded a $44.4 million contract by the U.S. <a title=\"Food and Drug Administration\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Food_and_Drug_Administration\">Food and Drug Administration</a>, boosting its shares by about 21%.<sup id=\"cite_ref-43\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Palantir_Technologies#cite_note-43\">[43]</a></sup></p>\r\n<h3><span id=\"Valuation\" class=\"mw-headline\">Valuation</span></h3>\r\n<p>The company was valued at $9 billion in early 2014, with <em><a title=\"Forbes\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Forbes\">Forbes</a></em> stating that the valuation made Palantir \"among <a title=\"Silicon Valley\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Silicon_Valley\">Silicon Valley</a>'s most valuable private technology companies\".<sup id=\"cite_ref-teafunding_32-4\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Palantir_Technologies#cite_note-teafunding-32\">[32]</a></sup> As of December 2014, Thiel was Palantir's largest shareholder.<sup id=\"cite_ref-teafunding_32-5\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Palantir_Technologies#cite_note-teafunding-32\">[32]</a></sup> In January 2015, the company was valued at $15 billion after an undisclosed round of funding with $50 million in November 2014.<sup id=\"cite_ref-44\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Palantir_Technologies#cite_note-44\">[44]</a></sup> This valuation rose to $20 billion in late 2015 as the company closed an $880 million round of funding.<sup id=\"cite_ref-20billion_45-0\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Palantir_Technologies#cite_note-20billion-45\">[45]</a></sup> Palantir has never reported a profit. In 2018, <a title=\"Morgan Stanley\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Morgan_Stanley\">Morgan Stanley</a> valued the company at $6 billion.<sup id=\"cite_ref-46\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Palantir_Technologies#cite_note-46\">[46]</a></sup></p>\r\n<p>Karp, Palantir's <a title=\"Chief executive officer\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chief_executive_officer\">chief executive officer</a>, announced in 2013 that the company would not pursue an <a class=\"mw-redirect\" title=\"IPO\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/IPO\">IPO</a>, as going public would make \"running a company like ours very difficult\".<sup id=\"cite_ref-teafunding_32-6\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Palantir_Technologies#cite_note-teafunding-32\">[32]</a></sup> However, on October 18, 2018, the <em><a class=\"mw-redirect\" title=\"Wall Street Journal\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wall_Street_Journal\">Wall Street Journal</a></em> reported that Palantir was considering an IPO in the first half of 2019 following a $41 billion valuation.<sup id=\"cite_ref-47\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Palantir_Technologies#cite_note-47\">[47]</a></sup> In July 2020, it was revealed the company had filed for an IPO.<sup id=\"cite_ref-48\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Palantir_Technologies#cite_note-48\">[48]</a></sup></p>\r\n<p>It ultimately went public on the New York Stock Exchange through a <a title=\"Direct public offering\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Direct_public_offering\">direct public offering</a> on September 30, 2020 under the ticker symbol \"PLTR\".<sup id=\"cite_ref-Kindig_2020_49-0\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Palantir_Technologies#cite_note-Kindig_2020-49\">[49]</a></sup></p>\r\n<h3><span id=\"Investments\" class=\"mw-headline\">Investments</span></h3>\r\n<p>The company has invested over $400 million into nearly two dozen <a title=\"Special-purpose acquisition company\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Special-purpose_acquisition_company\">SPAC</a> targets according to investment bank <a title=\"RBC Capital Markets\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/RBC_Capital_Markets\">RBC Capital Markets</a>, while bringing alongside those companies as customers.<sup id=\"cite_ref-50\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Palantir_Technologies#cite_note-50\">[50]</a></sup></p>\r\n<h2><span id=\"Products\" class=\"mw-headline\">Products</span></h2>\r\n<h3><span id=\"Palantir_Gotham\" class=\"mw-headline\">Palantir Gotham</span></h3>\r\n<p>Palantir Gotham is Palantir's government offering. It is an evolution of Palantir's longstanding work in the <a title=\"United States Intelligence Community\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States_Intelligence_Community\">United States Intelligence Community</a>. More recently, Palantir Gotham has been used as a <a title=\"Predictive policing\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Predictive_policing\">predictive policing</a> system, which has elicited some controversy over racism in their AI analytics.<sup id=\"cite_ref-AP_Pushback_51-0\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Palantir_Technologies#cite_note-AP_Pushback-51\">[51]</a></sup></p>\r\n<h3><span id=\"Palantir_Metropolis\" class=\"mw-headline\">Palantir Metropolis</span></h3>\r\n<p>Palantir Metropolis (formerly known as Palantir Finance) was<sup id=\"cite_ref-52\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Palantir_Technologies#cite_note-52\">[52]</a></sup><sup id=\"cite_ref-53\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Palantir_Technologies#cite_note-53\">[53]</a></sup> software for <a title=\"Data integration\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Data_integration\">data integration</a>, <a title=\"Information management\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Information_management\">information management</a> and quantitative <a title=\"Analytics\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Analytics\">analytics</a>. The software connects to commercial, proprietary and <a title=\"Public data\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Public_data\">public data</a> sets and discovers trends, relationships and anomalies, including <a title=\"Predictive analytics\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Predictive_analytics\">predictive analytics</a>.<sup id=\"cite_ref-Bloomberg180419Waldman_54-0\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Palantir_Technologies#cite_note-Bloomberg180419Waldman-54\">[54]</a></sup><sup id=\"cite_ref-Bloomberg180419Mak_55-0\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Palantir_Technologies#cite_note-Bloomberg180419Mak-55\">[55]</a></sup> Aided by 120 \"forward-deployed engineers\" of Palantir during 2009, Peter Cavicchia III of JPMorgan used Metropolis to monitor employee communications and alert the insider threat team when an employee showed any signs of potential disgruntlement: the insider alert team would further scrutinize the employee and possibly conduct physical surveillance after hours with bank security personnel.<sup id=\"cite_ref-Bloomberg180419Waldman_54-1\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Palantir_Technologies#cite_note-Bloomberg180419Waldman-54\">[54]</a></sup><sup id=\"cite_ref-Bloomberg180419Mak_55-1\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Palantir_Technologies#cite_note-Bloomberg180419Mak-55\">[55]</a></sup> The Metropolis team used emails, download activity, browser histories, and GPS locations from JPMorgan owned smartphones and their transcripts of digitally recorded phone conversations to search, aggregate, sort, and analyze this information for any specific keywords, phrases, and patterns of behavior.<sup id=\"cite_ref-Bloomberg180419Waldman_54-2\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Palantir_Technologies#cite_note-Bloomberg180419Waldman-54\">[54]</a></sup><sup id=\"cite_ref-Bloomberg180419Mak_55-2\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Palantir_Technologies#cite_note-Bloomberg180419Mak-55\">[55]</a></sup> In 2013, Cavicchia may have shared this information with <a title=\"Frank Bisignano\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Frank_Bisignano\">Frank Bisignano</a> who had become the CEO of <a class=\"mw-redirect\" title=\"First Data Corporation\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/First_Data_Corporation\">First Data Corporation</a>.<sup id=\"cite_ref-Bloomberg180419Waldman_54-3\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Palantir_Technologies#cite_note-Bloomberg180419Waldman-54\">[54]</a></sup></p>\r\n<h3><span id=\"Palantir_Apollo\" class=\"mw-headline\">Palantir Apollo</span></h3>\r\n<p>Palantir Apollo is a continuous delivery system that manages and deploys Palantir Gotham and Foundry.<sup id=\"cite_ref-56\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Palantir_Technologies#cite_note-56\">[56]</a></sup> Apollo was built out of the need for customers to use multiple public and private cloud platforms as part of their infrastructure. Apollo orchestrates updates to configurations and software in the Foundry and Gotham platforms using a <a title=\"Microservices\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Microservices\">micro-service</a> architecture. This product allows Palantir to provide software as a service (<a title=\"Software as a service\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Software_as_a_service\">SaaS</a>) rather than to operate as a consulting company.<sup id=\"cite_ref-57\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Palantir_Technologies#cite_note-57\">[57]</a></sup></p>\r\n<h3><span id=\"Palantir_Foundry\" class=\"mw-headline\">Palantir Foundry</span></h3>\r\n<p>Palantir Foundry was used by <a title=\"NHS England\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/NHS_England\">NHS England</a> in dealing with the <a title=\"COVID-19 pandemic in England\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/COVID-19_pandemic_in_England\">COVID-19 pandemic in England</a> to analyze the operation of the vaccination program. A campaign was started against the company in June 2021 by Foxglove, a tech-justice nonprofit, because \"Their background has generally been in contracts where people are harmed, not healed.\" <a class=\"mw-redirect\" title=\"Clive Lewis MP\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Clive_Lewis_MP\">Clive Lewis MP</a>, supporting the campaign said Palantir had an \"appalling track record.\"<sup id=\"cite_ref-CNBC_58-0\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Palantir_Technologies#cite_note-CNBC-58\">[58]</a></sup></p>\r\n<p>Foundry is also used for the administration of the UK <a title=\"Homes for Ukraine\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Homes_for_Ukraine\">Homes for Ukraine</a> program.<sup id=\"cite_ref-59\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Palantir_Technologies#cite_note-59\">[59]</a></sup> It gives caseworkers employed by local authorities access to data held by the <a title=\"Department for Levelling Up, Housing and Communities\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Department_for_Levelling_Up,_Housing_and_Communities\">Department for Levelling Up, Housing and Communities</a>, some of which is supplied by the UK <a title=\"Home Office\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Home_Office\">Home Office</a>.</p>\r\n<h3><span id=\"Other\" class=\"mw-headline\">Other</span></h3>\r\n<p>The company has been involved in a number of business and consumer products, designing in part or in whole. For example, in 2014, they premiered Insightics, which according to the <em><a class=\"mw-redirect\" title=\"Wall Street Journal\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wall_Street_Journal\">Wall Street Journal</a> </em> \"extracts customer spending and demographic information from merchants&rsquo; <a title=\"Credit history\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Credit_history\">credit-card records</a>.\" It was created in tandem with credit processing company <a title=\"First Data\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/First_Data\">First Data</a>.<sup id=\"cite_ref-tezfirstprofit_60-0\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Palantir_Technologies#cite_note-tezfirstprofit-60\">[60]</a></sup></p>\r\n<p>In April 2023, the company launched Artificial Intelligence Platform (AIP) which integrates <a title=\"Large language model\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Large_language_model\">large language models</a> into privately operated networks. The company demonstrated its use in war, where a military operator was able to deploy operations and receive responses via an AI <a title=\"Chatbot\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chatbot\">chatbot</a>.<sup id=\"cite_ref-61\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Palantir_Technologies#cite_note-61\">[61]</a></sup><sup id=\"cite_ref-62\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Palantir_Technologies#cite_note-62\">[62]</a></sup> Citing potential risks of <a title=\"Generative artificial intelligence\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Generative_artificial_intelligence\">generative artificial intelligence</a>, CEO Karp said that the product would not let the AI independently carry out targeting operations, requiring human oversight.<sup id=\"cite_ref-63\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Palantir_Technologies#cite_note-63\">[63]</a></sup></p>\r\n<h2><span id=\"Customers\" class=\"mw-headline\">Customers</span></h2>\r\n<h3><span id=\"Corporate_use\" class=\"mw-headline\">Corporate use</span></h3>\r\n<div class=\"hatnote navigation-not-searchable\" role=\"note\">See also: <a title=\"Information Warfare Monitor\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Information_Warfare_Monitor\">Information Warfare Monitor</a></div>\r\n<p>Palantir Metropolis is used by hedge funds, banks, and financial services firms.<sup id=\"cite_ref-bare_url_6-3\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Palantir_Technologies#cite_note-bare_url-6\">[6]</a></sup><sup id=\"cite_ref-npr_7-2\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Palantir_Technologies#cite_note-npr-7\">[7]</a></sup><sup id=\"cite_ref-bare_url_a_19-1\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Palantir_Technologies#cite_note-bare_url_a-19\">[19]</a></sup><sup id=\"cite_ref-64\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Palantir_Technologies#cite_note-64\">[64]</a></sup></p>\r\n<p>Palantir Foundry clients include <a class=\"mw-redirect\" title=\"Merck KGaA\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Merck_KGaA\">Merck KGaA</a>,<sup id=\"cite_ref-65\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Palantir_Technologies#cite_note-65\">[65]</a></sup> <a title=\"Airbus\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Airbus\">Airbus</a><sup id=\"cite_ref-66\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Palantir_Technologies#cite_note-66\">[66]</a></sup> and <a title=\"Scuderia Ferrari\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Scuderia_Ferrari\">Ferrari</a>.<sup id=\"cite_ref-67\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Palantir_Technologies#cite_note-67\">[67]</a></sup></p>\r\n<p>Palantir partner <a title=\"Information Warfare Monitor\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Information_Warfare_Monitor\">Information Warfare Monitor</a> used Palantir software to uncover both the <a class=\"mw-redirect\" title=\"Ghostnet\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ghostnet\">Ghostnet</a> and the <a title=\"Shadow Network\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Shadow_Network\">Shadow Network</a>.<sup id=\"cite_ref-bare_url_a_19-2\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Palantir_Technologies#cite_note-bare_url_a-19\">[19]</a></sup><sup id=\"cite_ref-68\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Palantir_Technologies#cite_note-68\">[68]</a></sup><sup id=\"cite_ref-Markoff_20-1\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Palantir_Technologies#cite_note-Markoff-20\">[20]</a></sup></p>\r\n<h3><span id=\"U.S._civil_entities\" class=\"mw-headline\">U.S. civil entities</span></h3>\r\n<p>Palantir's software is used by the <a title=\"Recovery Accountability and Transparency Board\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Recovery_Accountability_and_Transparency_Board\">Recovery Accountability and Transparency Board</a> to detect and investigate fraud and abuse in the <a class=\"mw-redirect\" title=\"American Recovery and Reinvestment Act\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/American_Recovery_and_Reinvestment_Act\">American Recovery and Reinvestment Act</a>. Specifically, the Recovery Operations Center (ROC) used Palantir to integrate transactional data with open-source and private data sets that describe the entities receiving stimulus funds.<sup class=\"noprint Inline-Template\" style=\"margin-left: 0.1em; white-space: nowrap;\">[<em><a title=\"Wikipedia:Please clarify\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia:Please_clarify\"><span title=\"The text near this tag may need clarification or removal of jargon. (March 2015)\">clarification needed</span></a></em>]</sup><sup id=\"cite_ref-bare_url_b_25-1\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Palantir_Technologies#cite_note-bare_url_b-25\">[25]</a></sup> Other clients as of 2019 included <a title=\"Polaris Project\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Polaris_Project\">Polaris Project</a>,<sup id=\"cite_ref-69\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Palantir_Technologies#cite_note-69\">[69]</a></sup> the <a title=\"Centers for Disease Control and Prevention\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Centers_for_Disease_Control_and_Prevention\">Centers for Disease Control and Prevention</a>, the <a class=\"mw-redirect\" title=\"National Center for Missing and Exploited Children\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/National_Center_for_Missing_and_Exploited_Children\">National Center for Missing and Exploited Children</a>,<sup id=\"cite_ref-tebtecnchrun_28-3\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Palantir_Technologies#cite_note-tebtecnchrun-28\">[28]</a></sup> the <a title=\"National Institutes of Health\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/National_Institutes_of_Health\">National Institutes of Health</a>,<sup id=\"cite_ref-70\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Palantir_Technologies#cite_note-70\">[70]</a></sup> <a title=\"Team Rubicon\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Team_Rubicon\">Team Rubicon</a>,<sup id=\"cite_ref-71\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Palantir_Technologies#cite_note-71\">[71]</a></sup> and the United Nations <a title=\"World Food Programme\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_Food_Programme\">World Food Programme</a>.<sup id=\"cite_ref-72\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Palantir_Technologies#cite_note-72\">[72]</a></sup></p>\r\n<p>In October 2020, Palantir began helping the federal government set up a system that will track the manufacture, distribution and administration of <a class=\"mw-redirect\" title=\"Coronavirus disease 2019\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Coronavirus_disease_2019\">COVID-19</a> vaccines across the country.<sup id=\"cite_ref-73\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Palantir_Technologies#cite_note-73\">[73]</a></sup></p>\r\n<h3><span id=\"U.S._military.2C_intelligence.2C_and_police\"></span><span id=\"U.S._military,_intelligence,_and_police\" class=\"mw-headline\">U.S. military, intelligence, and police</span></h3>\r\n<p>Palantir Gotham is used by counter-terrorism analysts at offices in the <a title=\"United States Intelligence Community\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States_Intelligence_Community\">United States Intelligence Community</a> and <a title=\"United States Department of Defense\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States_Department_of_Defense\">United States Department of Defense</a>, fraud investigators at the <a title=\"Recovery Accountability and Transparency Board\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Recovery_Accountability_and_Transparency_Board\">Recovery Accountability and Transparency Board</a>, and cyber analysts at <a title=\"Information Warfare Monitor\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Information_Warfare_Monitor\">Information Warfare Monitor</a> (responsible for the <a title=\"GhostNet\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/GhostNet\">GhostNet</a> and the <a title=\"Shadow Network\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Shadow_Network\">Shadow Network</a> investigation).</p>\r\n<p>Other clients as of 2013 included <a class=\"mw-redirect\" title=\"DHS\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/DHS\">DHS</a>, <a class=\"mw-redirect\" title=\"NSA\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/NSA\">NSA</a>, <a class=\"mw-redirect\" title=\"FBI\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/FBI\">FBI</a>, the <a title=\"United States Marine Corps\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States_Marine_Corps\">Marine Corps</a>, the <a title=\"United States Air Force\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States_Air_Force\">Air Force</a>, <a title=\"United States Special Operations Command\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States_Special_Operations_Command\">Special Operations Command</a>, <a class=\"mw-redirect\" title=\"West Point\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/West_Point\">West Point</a>, the <a class=\"mw-redirect\" title=\"Joint IED Defeat Organization\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Joint_IED_Defeat_Organization\">Joint IED Defeat Organization</a> and Allies. However, at the time the <a title=\"United States Army\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States_Army\">United States Army</a> continued to use its own data analysis tool.<sup id=\"cite_ref-tebtecnchrun_28-4\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Palantir_Technologies#cite_note-tebtecnchrun-28\">[28]</a></sup> Also, according to <a title=\"TechCrunch\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TechCrunch\">TechCrunch</a>, \"The U.S. spy agencies also employed Palantir to <a class=\"mw-redirect\" title=\"Database integration\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Database_integration\">connect databases</a> across departments. Before this, most of the databases used by the CIA and <a class=\"mw-redirect\" title=\"FBI\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/FBI\">FBI</a> were <a title=\"Information silo\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Information_silo\">siloed</a>, forcing users to search each database individually. Now everything is linked together using Palantir.\"<sup id=\"cite_ref-tebtecnchrun_28-5\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Palantir_Technologies#cite_note-tebtecnchrun-28\">[28]</a></sup></p>\r\n<p>U.S. <a title=\"Military intelligence\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Military_intelligence\">military intelligence</a> used the Palantir product to improve their ability to predict locations of <a class=\"mw-redirect\" title=\"Improvised explosive devices\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Improvised_explosive_devices\">improvised explosive devices</a> in its <a class=\"mw-redirect\" title=\"War in Afghanistan (2001&ndash;present)\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/War_in_Afghanistan_(2001%E2%80%93present)\">war in Afghanistan</a>. A small number of practitioners reported it to be more useful than the United States Army's <a class=\"mw-redirect\" title=\"Program of Record\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Program_of_Record\">Program of Record</a>, the <a title=\"Distributed Common Ground System\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Distributed_Common_Ground_System\">Distributed Common Ground System</a> (DCGS-A). California Congressman <a title=\"Duncan D. Hunter\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Duncan_D._Hunter\">Duncan D. Hunter</a> complained of <a title=\"United States Department of Defense\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States_Department_of_Defense\">United States Department of Defense</a> obstacles to its wider use in 2012.<sup id=\"cite_ref-74\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Palantir_Technologies#cite_note-74\">[74]</a></sup></p>\r\n<p>Palantir has also been reported to be working with various U.S. police departments, for example accepting a contract in 2013 to help the Northern California Regional Intelligence Center build a controversial <a class=\"mw-redirect\" title=\"License plate\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/License_plate\">license plates</a> database for California.<sup id=\"cite_ref-75\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Palantir_Technologies#cite_note-75\">[75]</a></sup> In 2012 <a title=\"New Orleans Police Department\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/New_Orleans_Police_Department\">New Orleans Police Department</a> partnered with Palantir to create a predictive policing program.<sup id=\"cite_ref-76\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Palantir_Technologies#cite_note-76\">[76]</a></sup></p>\r\n<p>In 2014, <a class=\"mw-redirect\" title=\"US Immigration and Customs Enforcement\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/US_Immigration_and_Customs_Enforcement\">US Immigration and Customs Enforcement</a> (ICE) awarded Palantir a $41 million contract to build and maintain a new intelligence system called Investigative Case Management (ICM) to track personal and criminal records of legal and <a class=\"mw-redirect\" title=\"Illegal immigrant\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Illegal_immigrant\">illegal immigrants</a>. This application has originally been conceived by ICE's office of Homeland Security Investigations (HSI), allowing its users access to intelligence platforms maintained by other federal and private law enforcement entities. The system reached its \"final operation capacity\" under the Trump administration in September 2017.<sup id=\"cite_ref-DeportationMachine_77-0\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Palantir_Technologies#cite_note-DeportationMachine-77\">[77]</a></sup></p>\r\n<p>Palantir took over the Pentagon's <a class=\"mw-redirect\" title=\"Project Maven\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Project_Maven\">Project Maven</a> contract in 2019 after Google decided not to continue developing AI unmanned drones used for bombings and intelligence.<sup id=\"cite_ref-:0_78-0\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Palantir_Technologies#cite_note-:0-78\">[78]</a></sup></p>\r\n<h3><span id=\"International_Atomic_Energy_Agency\" class=\"mw-headline\">International Atomic Energy Agency</span></h3>\r\n<p>Palantir was used by the <a title=\"International Atomic Energy Agency\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/International_Atomic_Energy_Agency\">International Atomic Energy Agency (IAEA)</a> to verify if Iran was in compliance with the <a title=\"Iran nuclear deal framework\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iran_nuclear_deal_framework\">2015 agreement</a>.<sup id=\"cite_ref-IranNuclearDeal_33-1\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Palantir_Technologies#cite_note-IranNuclearDeal-33\">[33]</a></sup></p>\r\n<h3><span id=\"British_National_Health_Service_.28NHS.29\"></span><span id=\"British_National_Health_Service_(NHS)\" class=\"mw-headline\">British National Health Service (NHS)</span></h3>\r\n<p>The firm has contracts relating to patient data from the British <a title=\"National Health Service\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/National_Health_Service\">National Health Service</a>. It was awarded an emergency, no-competition contract to mine COVID-19 patient data in 2019. In 2020 this was valued at more than &pound;23.5 million and was extended for two more years. The awarding of the contract without competition was heavily criticised, prompting the NHS to pledge an open and transparent procurement process for any future data contract.<sup id=\"cite_ref-79\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Palantir_Technologies#cite_note-79\">[79]</a></sup><sup id=\"cite_ref-80\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Palantir_Technologies#cite_note-80\">[80]</a></sup></p>\r\n<p>The firm was encouraged by <a title=\"Liam Fox\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Liam_Fox\">Liam Fox</a> \"to expand their software business\" in Britain.<sup id=\"cite_ref-81\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Palantir_Technologies#cite_note-81\">[81]</a></sup> It was said to be \"critical to the success of the vaccination and PPE programmes,&rdquo; but its involvement in the NHS was controversial among civil liberties groups.<sup id=\"cite_ref-82\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Palantir_Technologies#cite_note-82\">[82]</a></sup> Conservative MP <a title=\"David Davis (British politician)\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/David_Davis_(British_politician)\">David Davis</a> called for a judicial review into the sharing of patient data with Palantir.<sup id=\"cite_ref-83\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Palantir_Technologies#cite_note-83\">[83]</a></sup></p>\r\n<p>The procurement of a &pound;480m Federated Data Platform by <a title=\"NHS England\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/NHS_England\">NHS England</a>, launched in January 2023 has been described as a 'must win' for Palantir.<sup id=\"cite_ref-84\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Palantir_Technologies#cite_note-84\">[84]</a></sup> The procurement has been described as a \"farce\" by civil liberties campaigners, alleging that Palantir have a competitive advantage as it \"already has its feet under the table in NHS England\" and benefits from a short procurement window.<sup id=\"cite_ref-85\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Palantir_Technologies#cite_note-85\">[85]</a></sup> In April 2023 it was revealed that a consortium of UK companies had been unsuccessful in its bid for the contract.<sup id=\"cite_ref-86\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Palantir_Technologies#cite_note-86\">[86]</a></sup></p>\r\n<p>In April 2023, Conservative MP David Davis publicly expressed his concern over the procurement process, stating that it could become a \"battle royale\". Davis is one of a dozen MPs pressing the government over privacy concerns with the use of data. Labour peer and former Health Minister <a title=\"Philip Hunt, Baron Hunt of Kings Heath\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Philip_Hunt,_Baron_Hunt_of_Kings_Heath\">Philip Hunt</a> voiced his concern about Palantir's use of data, stating &ldquo;The current NHS and current government doesn&rsquo;t have a good track record of getting the details right, and the procurement shows no sign of going better.&rdquo; <sup id=\"cite_ref-Mason_87-0\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Palantir_Technologies#cite_note-Mason-87\">[87]</a></sup></p>\r\n<p>In April 2023, it was also reported that Palantir had seen eleven pilots of its Foundry system paused by NHS organisations. A spokesperson for the Department of Health and Social Care stated that this was due to \"operational issues\".<sup id=\"cite_ref-Mason_87-1\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Palantir_Technologies#cite_note-Mason-87\">[87]</a></sup></p>\r\n<p>In January 2023 Palantir's founder, <a title=\"Peter Thiel\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Peter_Thiel\">Peter Thiel</a>, called Britain's affection for the NHS \"<a title=\"Stockholm syndrome\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Stockholm_syndrome\">Stockholm Syndrome</a>\" during a speech to the <a title=\"Oxford Union\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Oxford_Union\">Oxford Union</a>, going on to say that the NHS \"makes people sick\". A Palantir spokesman clarified that Thiel was \"speaking as a private individual\" and his comments \"do not in any way reflect the views of Palantir\".<sup id=\"cite_ref-88\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Palantir_Technologies#cite_note-88\">[88]</a></sup></p>\r\n<p>In March 2023 it was revealed that NHS hospitals had been 'ordered' to share patient data with Palantir, prompting renewed criticism from civil liberties groups.<sup id=\"cite_ref-89\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Palantir_Technologies#cite_note-89\">[89]</a></sup> Campaign groups including the <a title=\"The Doctors' Association UK\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_Doctors%27_Association_UK\">Doctors' Association UK</a>, <a title=\"National Pensioners Convention\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/National_Pensioners_Convention\">National Pensioners' Convention</a>, and Just Treatment, subsequently threatened legal action over NHS England's procurement of the FDP contract citing concerns over the use of patient data.<sup id=\"cite_ref-90\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Palantir_Technologies#cite_note-90\">[90]</a></sup></p>\r\n<p><a title=\"NHS England\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/NHS_England\">NHS England</a>'s former artificial intelligence chief, Indra Joshi, was recruited by Palantir in 2022. The company said they were planning to increase their team in the UK by 250.<sup id=\"cite_ref-91\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Palantir_Technologies#cite_note-91\">[91]</a></sup> Palantir's UK head, Louis Moseley, was quoted internally as saying that Palantir's strategy for entry into the British health industry was to \"Buy our way in\" by hoovering up smaller rival companies with existing relationships with the NHS in order to &ldquo;take a lot of ground and take down a lot of political resistance.&rdquo; <sup id=\"cite_ref-92\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Palantir_Technologies#cite_note-92\">[92]</a></sup></p>\r\n<h3><span id=\"Europe\" class=\"mw-headline\">Europe</span></h3>\r\n<p>The Danish POL-INTEL predictive policing project has been operational since 2017 and is based on the Gotham system. According to the AP the Danish system \"uses a mapping system to build a so-called heat map identifying areas with higher crime rates.\" The Gotham system has also been used by German state police in Hesse and Europol.<sup id=\"cite_ref-AP_Pushback_51-1\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Palantir_Technologies#cite_note-AP_Pushback-51\">[51]</a></sup></p>\r\n<p>The Norwegian Customs is using Palantir Gotham to screen passengers and vehicles for control. Known inputs are prefiled freight documents, passenger lists, the national Currency Exchange database (tracks all cross-border currency exchanges), the Norwegian Welfare Administrations employer- and employee-registry, the Norwegian stock holder registry and 30 public databases from InfoTorg. InfoTorg provides access to more than 30 databases, including the Norwegian National Citizen registry, European Business Register, the Norwegian DMV vehicle registry, various credit databases etc. These databases are supplemented by the Norwegian Customs Departments own intelligence reports, including results of previous controls. The system is also augmented by data from public sources such as social media.<sup id=\"cite_ref-93\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Palantir_Technologies#cite_note-93\">[93]</a></sup></p>\r\n<div class=\"thumb tright\">\r\n<div class=\"thumbinner\" style=\"width: 222px;\"><a class=\"image\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Palantir_2022.jpg\"><img class=\"thumbimage\" src=\"https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/86/Palantir_2022.jpg/220px-Palantir_2022.jpg\" srcset=\"//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/86/Palantir_2022.jpg/330px-Palantir_2022.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/86/Palantir_2022.jpg/440px-Palantir_2022.jpg 2x\" width=\"220\" height=\"140\" data-file-width=\"3208\" data-file-height=\"2047\"></a>\r\n<div class=\"thumbcaption\">\r\n<div class=\"magnify\">&nbsp;</div>\r\n</div>\r\n</div>\r\n</div>\r\n<div class=\"thumb tright\">\r\n<div class=\"thumbinner\" style=\"width: 222px;\">\r\n<div class=\"thumbcaption\">Palantir stand at the NHS Confederation conference 2022</div>\r\n</div>\r\n</div>\r\n<h4><span id=\"Ukraine\" class=\"mw-headline\">Ukraine</span></h4>\r\n<p>Palantir's technology is used close to the front line. It is used to shorten the \"<a title=\"Kill chain\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kill_chain\">kill chain</a>\" in <a title=\"Russo-Ukrainian War\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Russo-Ukrainian_War\">Russo-Ukrainian War</a>.<sup id=\"cite_ref-94\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Palantir_Technologies#cite_note-94\">[94]</a></sup> According to a December 2022 report by <em><a title=\"The Times\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_Times\">The Times</a></em>, Palantir's AI has allowed Ukraine to increase the accuracy, speed, and deadliness of its artillery strikes despite having a fraction of the artillery forces.<sup id=\"cite_ref-95\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Palantir_Technologies#cite_note-95\">[95]</a></sup> <a title=\"Prosecutor General of Ukraine\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Prosecutor_General_of_Ukraine\">Ukraine's prosecutor general's office</a> also planned to utilize Palantir's software to help it prosecute alleged <a title=\"War crimes in the Russian invasion of Ukraine\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/War_crimes_in_the_Russian_invasion_of_Ukraine\">war crimes in the Russian invasion of Ukraine</a>.<sup id=\"cite_ref-96\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Palantir_Technologies#cite_note-96\">[96]</a></sup></p>\r\n<h2><span id=\"Partnerships_and_contracts\" class=\"mw-headline\">Partnerships and contracts</span></h2>\r\n<h3><span id=\"International_Business_Machines\" class=\"mw-headline\">International Business Machines</span></h3>\r\n<p>On February 8, 2021, Palantir and IBM announced a new partnership that would use IBM's hybrid cloud data platform alongside Palantir's operations platform for building applications. The product, Palantir for IBM Cloud Pak for Data, is expected to simplify the process of building and deploying AI-integrated applications with IBM Watson. It will help businesses/users interpret and use large datasets without needing a strong technical background. Palantir for IBM Cloud Pak for Data will be available for general use in March 2021.<sup id=\"cite_ref-97\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Palantir_Technologies#cite_note-97\">[97]</a></sup></p>\r\n<h3><span id=\"Amazon_.28AWS.29\"></span><span id=\"Amazon_(AWS)\" class=\"mw-headline\">Amazon (AWS)</span></h3>\r\n<p>On March 5, 2021, Palantir announced its partnership with Amazon AWS. Palantir's ERP Suite is now optimized to run on <a title=\"Amazon Web Services\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Amazon_Web_Services\">Amazon Web Services</a>. One of the first notable successes of the ERP suite was with <a title=\"BP\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/BP\">BP</a>, which was able to save about $50 million in working capital within two weeks of onboarding the system.<sup id=\"cite_ref-98\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Palantir_Technologies#cite_note-98\">[98]</a></sup></p>\r\n<h3><span id=\"Babylon_Health\" class=\"mw-headline\">Babylon Health</span></h3>\r\n<p>Palantir took a stake in <a title=\"Babylon Health\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Babylon_Health\">Babylon Health</a> in June 2021. <a title=\"Ali Parsa\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ali_Parsa\">Ali Parsa</a> told the <em><a title=\"Financial Times\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Financial_Times\">Financial Times</a></em> that \"nobody\" has brought some of the tech that Palantir owns \"into the realm of biology and health care\".<sup id=\"cite_ref-CNBC_58-1\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Palantir_Technologies#cite_note-CNBC-58\">[58]</a></sup></p>\r\n<h2><span id=\"Controversies\" class=\"mw-headline\">Controversies</span></h2>\r\n<h3><span id=\"Algorithm_development\" class=\"mw-headline\">Algorithm development</span></h3>\r\n<p><a title=\"I2 Group\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/I2_Group\">i2 Inc</a> sued Palantir in Federal Court alleging fraud, conspiracy, and copyright infringement over Palantir's algorithm. Shyam Sankar, Palantir's director of business development, used a <a title=\"Private investigator\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Private_investigator\">private eye</a> company as the <a title=\"Cutout (espionage)\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cutout_(espionage)\">cutout</a> for obtaining i2's code. i2 settled out of court for $10 million in 2011.<sup id=\"cite_ref-Bloomberg180419Waldman_54-4\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Palantir_Technologies#cite_note-Bloomberg180419Waldman-54\">[54]</a></sup></p>\r\n<h3><span id=\"WikiLeaks_proposals_.282010.29\"></span><span id=\"WikiLeaks_proposals_(2010)\" class=\"mw-headline\">WikiLeaks proposals (2010)</span></h3>\r\n<p>In 2010, <a class=\"mw-redirect\" title=\"Hunton &amp; Williams\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hunton_%26_Williams\">Hunton &amp; Williams</a> LLP allegedly asked <a title=\"Berico Technologies\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Berico_Technologies\">Berico Technologies</a>, Palantir, and <a class=\"mw-redirect\" title=\"HBGary Federal\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/HBGary_Federal\">HBGary Federal</a> to draft a response plan to \"the <a title=\"WikiLeaks\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/WikiLeaks\">WikiLeaks</a> Threat.\" In early 2011 <a class=\"mw-redirect\" title=\"Anonymous (group)\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Anonymous_(group)\">Anonymous</a> publicly released HBGary-internal documents, including the plan. The plan proposed that Palantir software would \"serve as the foundation for all the data collection, integration, analysis, and production efforts.\"<sup id=\"cite_ref-Harris_99-0\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Palantir_Technologies#cite_note-Harris-99\">[99]</a></sup> The plan also included slides, allegedly authored by HBGary CEO Aaron Barr, which suggested \"[spreading] disinformation\" and \"disrupting\" <a title=\"Glenn Greenwald\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glenn_Greenwald\">Glenn Greenwald</a>&rsquo;s support for WikiLeaks.<sup id=\"cite_ref-100\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Palantir_Technologies#cite_note-100\">[100]</a></sup></p>\r\n<p>Palantir CEO Karp ended all ties to HBGary and issued a statement apologizing to \"progressive organizations&hellip; and Greenwald &hellip; for any involvement that we may have had in these matters.\" Palantir placed an employee on leave pending a review by a third-party law firm. The employee was later reinstated.<sup id=\"cite_ref-Harris_99-1\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Palantir_Technologies#cite_note-Harris-99\">[99]</a></sup></p>\r\n<h3><span id=\"Racial_discrimination_lawsuit_.282016.29\"></span><span id=\"Racial_discrimination_lawsuit_(2016)\" class=\"mw-headline\">Racial discrimination lawsuit (2016)</span></h3>\r\n<p>On September 26, 2016, the <a title=\"Office of Federal Contract Compliance Programs\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Office_of_Federal_Contract_Compliance_Programs\">Office of Federal Contract Compliance Programs</a> of the <a title=\"United States Department of Labor\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States_Department_of_Labor\">U.S. Department of Labor</a> filed a lawsuit against Palantir alleging that the company discriminated against Asian job applicants on the basis of their race.<sup id=\"cite_ref-101\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Palantir_Technologies#cite_note-101\">[101]</a></sup> According to the lawsuit, the company \"routinely eliminated\" Asian applicants during the hiring process, even when they were \"as qualified as white applicants\" for the same jobs.<sup id=\"cite_ref-vanityfair_102-0\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Palantir_Technologies#cite_note-vanityfair-102\">[102]</a></sup> Palantir settled the suit in April 2017 for $1.7 million while not admitting wrongdoing.<sup id=\"cite_ref-103\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Palantir_Technologies#cite_note-103\">[103]</a></sup></p>\r\n<h3><span id=\"British_Parliament_inquiry_.282018.29\"></span><span id=\"British_Parliament_inquiry_(2018)\" class=\"mw-headline\">British Parliament inquiry (2018)</span></h3>\r\n<p>During questioning in front of the <a class=\"mw-redirect\" title=\"Digital, Culture, Media and Sport Committee\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Digital,_Culture,_Media_and_Sport_Committee\">Digital, Culture, Media and Sport Select Committee</a>, <a title=\"Christopher Wylie\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Christopher_Wylie\">Christopher Wylie</a>, the former research director of <a title=\"Cambridge Analytica\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cambridge_Analytica\">Cambridge Analytica</a>, said that several meetings had taken place between Palantir and Cambridge Analytica, and that Alexander Nix, the chief executive of <a title=\"SCL Group\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/SCL_Group\">SCL</a>, had facilitated their use of <a title=\"Aleksandr Kogan (scientist)\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Aleksandr_Kogan_(scientist)\">Aleksandr Kogan</a>'s data which had been obtained from his app \"thisisyourdigitallife\" by mining personal surveys. Kogan later established Global Science Research to share the data with Cambridge Analytica and others. Wylie confirmed that both employees from Cambridge Analytica and Palantir used Kogan's Global Science Research and harvested Facebook data together in the same offices.<sup id=\"cite_ref-Guardian180327Pegg_104-0\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Palantir_Technologies#cite_note-Guardian180327Pegg-104\">[104]</a></sup><sup id=\"cite_ref-NYT180327_105-0\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Palantir_Technologies#cite_note-NYT180327-105\">[105]</a></sup></p>\r\n<h3><span id=\"ICE_partnership_.28since_2014.29\"></span><span id=\"ICE_partnership_(since_2014)\" class=\"mw-headline\">ICE partnership (since 2014)</span></h3>\r\n<p>Palantir has come under criticism due to its partnership developing software for <a title=\"U.S. Immigration and Customs Enforcement\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/U.S._Immigration_and_Customs_Enforcement\">U.S. Immigration and Customs Enforcement</a>. Palantir has responded that its software is not used to facilitate deportations. In a statement provided to the New York Times,<sup id=\"cite_ref-106\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Palantir_Technologies#cite_note-106\">[106]</a></sup> the firm implied that because its contract was with HSI, a division of ICE focused on investigating criminal activities, it played no role in deportations. However, documents obtained by <em><a title=\"The Intercept\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_Intercept\">The Intercept</a></em><sup id=\"cite_ref-DeportationMachine_77-1\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Palantir_Technologies#cite_note-DeportationMachine-77\">[77]</a></sup> show that this is not the case. According to these documents, Palantir's ICM software is considered 'mission critical' to ICE. Other groups critical of Palantir include the <a title=\"Brennan Center for Justice\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Brennan_Center_for_Justice\">Brennan Center for Justice</a>,<sup id=\"cite_ref-107\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Palantir_Technologies#cite_note-107\">[107]</a></sup> National Immigration Project,<sup id=\"cite_ref-108\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Palantir_Technologies#cite_note-108\">[108]</a></sup> the Immigrant Defense Project,<sup id=\"cite_ref-109\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Palantir_Technologies#cite_note-109\">[109]</a></sup> the <a title=\"Tech Workers Coalition\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tech_Workers_Coalition\">Tech Workers Coalition</a> and Mijente.<sup id=\"cite_ref-110\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Palantir_Technologies#cite_note-110\">[110]</a></sup> In one internal ICE report<sup id=\"cite_ref-111\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Palantir_Technologies#cite_note-111\">[111]</a></sup> Mijente acquired, it was revealed that Palantir's software was critical in an operation to arrest the parents of undocumented migrant children.</p>\r\n<p>On September 28, 2020, <a title=\"Amnesty International\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Amnesty_International\">Amnesty International</a> released a report criticizing Palantir failure to conduct human rights due diligence around its contracts with <a title=\"U.S. Immigration and Customs Enforcement\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/U.S._Immigration_and_Customs_Enforcement\">ICE</a>. Concerns around Palantir's rights record were being scrutinized for contributing to <a class=\"mw-redirect\" title=\"Human rights violations\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human_rights_violations\">human rights violations</a> of <a class=\"mw-redirect\" title=\"Asylum-seekers\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Asylum-seekers\">asylum-seekers</a> and <a title=\"Economic migrant\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Economic_migrant\">migrants</a>.<sup id=\"cite_ref-112\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Palantir_Technologies#cite_note-112\">[112]</a></sup><sup id=\"cite_ref-113\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Palantir_Technologies#cite_note-113\">[113]</a></sup></p>\r\n<h3><span id=\".22HHS_Protect_Now.22_and_privacy_concerns_.28since_2020.29\"></span><span id=\"&quot;HHS_Protect_Now&quot;_and_privacy_concerns_(since_2020)\" class=\"mw-headline\">\"HHS Protect Now\" and privacy concerns (since 2020)</span></h3>\r\n<table class=\"box-Unbalanced_section plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content\" role=\"presentation\">\r\n<tbody>\r\n<tr>\r\n<td class=\"mbox-image\">\r\n<div class=\"mbox-image-div\"><img src=\"https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/Unbalanced_scales.svg/45px-Unbalanced_scales.svg.png\" srcset=\"//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/Unbalanced_scales.svg/68px-Unbalanced_scales.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/Unbalanced_scales.svg/90px-Unbalanced_scales.svg.png 2x\" alt=\"Unbalanced scales.svg\" width=\"45\" height=\"40\" data-file-width=\"400\" data-file-height=\"354\"></div>\r\n</td>\r\n<td class=\"mbox-text\">\r\n<div class=\"mbox-text-span\">This section <strong>may be <a class=\"mw-redirect\" title=\"Wikipedia:DUE\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia:DUE\">unbalanced</a> towards certain viewpoints</strong>.<span class=\"hide-when-compact\"> Please <a class=\"external text\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Palantir_Technologies&amp;action=edit\">improve the article</a> or discuss the issue on the <a title=\"Talk:Palantir Technologies\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Talk:Palantir_Technologies\">talk page</a>.</span> <span class=\"date-container\"><em>(<span class=\"date\">December 2020</span>)</em></span></div>\r\n</td>\r\n</tr>\r\n</tbody>\r\n</table>\r\n<p>The ongoing <a title=\"COVID-19 pandemic\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/COVID-19_pandemic\">COVID-19 pandemic</a> has prompted tech companies to respond to growing demand for citizen information from governments in order to conduct contact tracing and to analyze patient data.<sup id=\"cite_ref-114\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Palantir_Technologies#cite_note-114\">[114]</a></sup> Consequently, data collection companies, such as Palantir, have been contracted to partake in pandemic data collection practices. Palantir's participation in \"HHS Protect Now\", a program launched by the <a title=\"United States Department of Health and Human Services\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States_Department_of_Health_and_Human_Services\">United States Department of Health and Human Services</a> to track the spread of the coronavirus, has attracted criticism from American lawmakers.<sup id=\"cite_ref-Albergotti_115-0\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Palantir_Technologies#cite_note-Albergotti-115\">[115]</a></sup></p>\r\n<p>Palantir's participation in COVID-19 response projects re-ignited debates over its controversial involvement in tracking undocumented immigrants, especially its alleged effects on digital inequality and potential restrictions on online freedoms.
